  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1dc02242-9d0a-4f27-8673-f74b0f3cbdfb'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer17386207946537066449">Emma Swan's life has been anything but a fairy tale.   <span id="freeText17386207946537066449" style="display:none">Emma Swan's life has been anything but a fairy tale. She's been on her own since she was abandoned as a baby—that is, until the night of her twenty-eighth birthday, when Henry, a ten-year-old boy, shows up on her doorstep. He's the son Emma gave up for adoption, and this surprise visit turns her life upside down.<br /><br />Henry takes Emma back to his home in Storybrooke, Maine, where, Henry claims, all the residents are actually fairy tale characters who can't remember their true identities. And if Henry's right, that means that his sweet-natured, lonely schoolteacher Mary Margaret Blanchard is really Snow White, the iconic princess ... and also Emma's long-lost mother.<br /><br />In Fairy Tale Land, we meet Snow White as a bandit on the run, forced into exile by her stepmother, the Evil Queen. Snow's a young woman learning to become a hero, who will do anything to live happily ever after with her one true love, Prince Charming.<br /><br />The closer Emma comes to Henry in Storybrooke, the harder it is for her to ignore the dark curse that haunts this small New England town and binds her to Mary Margaret. If Emma can learn to accept her destiny as Storybrooke's savior and break the curse, she just might get the family reunion she's dreamed about her entire life.</span>

<div id="review_599038805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/599038805" />
    <a title="ShingetsuMoon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13246535-shingetsumoon"><img alt="ShingetsuMoon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474061046p2/13246535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/599038805?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ShingetsuMoon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ShingetsuMoon" href="/user/show/13246535-shingetsumoon">ShingetsuMoon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13246535-shingetsumoon?shelf=fairy-tales-and-similar-stories">fairy-tales-and-similar-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer599038805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15531435157455951165">The show (not quite) in book form. The book primarily focuses on what happens in Storybrooke and switches between Emma and Mary Margaret's point of view. So pretty much all of the major events that happen in Storybrooke during the show are in here. <br/><br/>Of course just for the sake of space they couldn't put everything in. Some moments are shortened, quickly glossed over, or explained by Henry, but not in a way that makes it feel rushed. And, yes, Jefferson gets his 5 minutes of fame as well.<br/><br/>However, </span>
  <span id="freeText15531435157455951165" style="display:none">The show (not quite) in book form. The book primarily focuses on what happens in Storybrooke and switches between Emma and Mary Margaret's point of view. So pretty much all of the major events that happen in Storybrooke during the show are in here. <br /><br />Of course just for the sake of space they couldn't put everything in. Some moments are shortened, quickly glossed over, or explained by Henry, but not in a way that makes it feel rushed. And, yes, Jefferson gets his 5 minutes of fame as well.<br /><br />However, they do delve into Fairy Tale Land to tell some parts of the story concerning Snow White, Charming, and Red Riding Hood. I was pleasantly surprised to see Ruby/Red's story included and not quickly explained as some others were.<br /><br />It also reminded me of how annoying David was when he was cursed (I'm so glad the curse was broken and he returned to "normal") and also how hard Mary Margaret really did try to do the right thing and stay away from him. Not just for her sake but Kathryn's as well.<br /><br />Also Mary Margaret's musings about Dr Whale were priceless. Seriously I recommend buying the book just for that alone.<br /><br />Highly recommended not just for dedicated fans of the show but for new fans as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15531435157455951165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_613270378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613270378" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11081406-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475027153p2/11081406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/613270378?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/11081406-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613270378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18175256388603449362">I fricking love Once Upon a Time. That show makes me feel all the feels. This book I have problems with. I've read fanfiction that's better written (and waay better edited - I highlighted no less than twelve mistakes). Also, they left out several episodes (the Hansel and Gretel story - The Still Small Voice, the Fruit of the Posionous Tree, etc). Also, limiting the narrative perspectives to just Emma and Mary Margaret (and Grumpy for a brief time) really took away from the complexity of the Once</span>
  <span id="freeText18175256388603449362" style="display:none">I fricking love Once Upon a Time. That show makes me feel all the feels. This book I have problems with. I've read fanfiction that's better written (and waay better edited - I highlighted no less than twelve mistakes). Also, they left out several episodes (the Hansel and Gretel story - The Still Small Voice, the Fruit of the Posionous Tree, etc). Also, limiting the narrative perspectives to just Emma and Mary Margaret (and Grumpy for a brief time) really took away from the complexity of the Once universe. Plus there was little to no Mr. Gold, who, as the fangirls know, is the best character. The writing is...not good. Very "tell tell tell, never show, if you wanted show, watch the actual show!" type of writing. But still, for a "I'm bored and I need something quick and enjoyable to read that isn't a thousand pages of A Song of Ice and Fire" kind of day. Now I must re-watch season 1 of Once and feel all the feels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18175256388603449362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2816955-francisca-viegas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099365899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17210920429414708793">I don't know exactly what I was expecting when I started reading this book, but it kind of took me by surprise.<br/>First of all, Once Upon a Time is one of my favourite series. I am totally in love with retellings, and even if the plot is kind of getting old and predictable, I still find it fun to watch.<br/>Reawakened was sort of a guide to the series. We get a little more insight on the reasons behind Emma and Snow's (or Mary Margaret's) decisions, but it's actually pretty disappointing as a stand alon</span>
  <span id="freeText17210920429414708793" style="display:none">I don't know exactly what I was expecting when I started reading this book, but it kind of took me by surprise.<br />First of all, Once Upon a Time is one of my favourite series. I am totally in love with retellings, and even if the plot is kind of getting old and predictable, I still find it fun to watch.<br />Reawakened was sort of a guide to the series. We get a little more insight on the reasons behind Emma and Snow's (or Mary Margaret's) decisions, but it's actually pretty disappointing as a stand alone book.<br />I guess you <i>could</i> read the book without watching or having watched the first season of OUaT, but if you did, you might find it very confusing and not at all explanatory. Lots of things happen in the series that lead to the final events, and most of these (especially the ones related to Rumplestiltskin) are not even mentioned.<br /><br />Having said this, my advice is: <b> do NOT read this book unless you saw the first season of the series.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17210920429414708793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8121350636546862073"><i>Reawakened</i> by Odette Beane follows Emma's journey over the course of the first season of ABC's <i>Once Upon A Time</i>. Each chapter is named after an episode - only five, I believe, are entirely eliminated. Of course, they couldn't fit everything in, so for the most part this book is set in Storybrooke with limited perspectives from Emma and Mary Margaret with a few key fairybacks to really set the tone and to show the importance of Operation Cobra. <br/><br/>I was pleased to see Snow and Charming, the Evil Que</span>
  <span id="freeText8121350636546862073" style="display:none"><i>Reawakened</i> by Odette Beane follows Emma's journey over the course of the first season of ABC's <i>Once Upon A Time</i>. Each chapter is named after an episode - only five, I believe, are entirely eliminated. Of course, they couldn't fit everything in, so for the most part this book is set in Storybrooke with limited perspectives from Emma and Mary Margaret with a few key fairybacks to really set the tone and to show the importance of Operation Cobra. <br><br>I was pleased to see Snow and Charming, the Evil Queen, and Red get their backstories fairly well explored. It really reminded me of how much I enjoyed Sheriff Graham/ the Huntsman and Jefferson/ the Mad Hatter. It's a pretty decent companion considering some elements were rushed, glossed over, or skipped. I recommend it if you're a fan of the tv series, or, perhaps, if you're considering starting to watch the series. However, I'd much rather watch the show. <i>Reawakened</i> definitely reminded me of how much I'd like to rewatch the first season. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451872508ra/17615447.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <span id="freeText17923894027456988720" style="display:none"><b> All you have to do is BELIEVE in the magic!</b><br><br><i>Once upon a time</i>…<br><br><b>All her life Emma had been a skeptic. She’d been the person who poked holes in other people’s logic, the person who saw through the illusions that trapped everyone else. <br>This time, though, it was different. <br>This time she’d been the one living in the dream world. <br>Emma, the realist, had been utterly wrong. </b><br><br><br>Once upon a time there was an enchanted forest filled with all the classic fairy tale characters we know. <br>Or we think we know. <br>One day they found themselves trapped in a place where all their happy endings were stolen. Our world. This is the tale of what happened and how true love’s kiss broke the spell… <br><br><br>{Based on the hit channel 5 series} <i>Once upon a time</i> is a remarkably clever, twisted narrative that deftly interweaves classic fairy tales within a contemporary façade. Prepare to lose yourself {and possibly your sanity!} within an intricate labyrinth of dark deceptions, mysterious wonders and shocking secrets. Perfectly imagined and written, It’s so easy to become spellbound by the irresistible romance and captivating plot. <br><br><br>At its core <b>reawakened</b> is a tale of hope. Through the spunky main protagonist, as a reader you are able to find your true self. When there are no Fairy Godmothers in the world nor magical potions, you are challenged to make changes and trust that innate <i>instinct</i>, so as to stand-up for our own beliefs. Irrevocably we have to try our best to create opportunities for ourselves because we are never going to get anything out of life if we don’t make an effort. We all long for a magical solution to our problems, yet sometimes astonishing tenacity can be hidden within the most unlikely of places. <br><br><br>True love isn’t easy. Neither is exposing the secrets of the soul, which dwell within the darkest corners of the heart. <br><br>In stories. As in life. Adversity teaches us things we cannot learn otherwise. Adversity helps to develop a depth of character that comes in no other way, than through perspicacity and comprehension. With perpetual change and challenge, one seeks the wisdom to realise joy and serenity. <br><br><b>Sometimes you can’t see yourself clearly until you see yourself through the eyes of others</b> <br><br>Complete with a compelling cast of complex characters this deliciously addictive, magical tale is one that transcends boundaries with eccentricity, originality and atypical incongruity! <br><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2qaq068" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_908244223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/908244223" />
    <a title="Jessica (Books: A true story)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113710-jessica-books-a-true-story"><img alt="Jessica (Books: A true story)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498713175p2/1113710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/908244223?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (Books: A true story)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (Books: A true story)" href="/user/show/1113710-jessica-books-a-true-story">Jessica (Books: A true story)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113710-jessica-books-a-true-story?shelf=library-2015">library-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113710-jessica-books-a-true-story?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113710-jessica-books-a-true-story?shelf=dnf-2015">dnf-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer908244223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9980644701452073153">I didn't know going into this that it was a novelization. I thought it was a bonus story that hadn't made it into the show. When I found it was just a novelization of Once Upon a Time Season 1, I still thought I would give it a try since that is my favorite show right now. This novelization felt really crammed because an entire TV season was smashed into this short, 337 page novel. There was a lot of telling. Conversations were sometimes summarized which is kind of boring to read. There were som</span>
  <span id="freeText9980644701452073153" style="display:none">I didn't know going into this that it was a novelization. I thought it was a bonus story that hadn't made it into the show. When I found it was just a novelization of Once Upon a Time Season 1, I still thought I would give it a try since that is my favorite show right now. This novelization felt really crammed because an entire TV season was smashed into this short, 337 page novel. There was a lot of telling. Conversations were sometimes summarized which is kind of boring to read. There were some insights into the character's thinking, but it felt like stuff I already knew or guessed at from watching the show. I quit at just over halfway on page 170. <br /><br />The chapter titles felt familiar to me so I looked them up. They are the episode titles. The novelization even skips some of the episodes which surprised me. I can't imagine how much telling there would have been if they had fit all the episodes in there.<br /><br />I understand it's a novelization and I shouldn't expect amazing writing, but there was not much I was getting out of it that was new or interesting. Usually when I read a novelization it either fills in details and expands the story or it's an immersive reliving of my favorite show. But this one did neither. There wasn't much insight into the characters or new story lines and there was so much to fit inside the novel that it felt like I was being told way too much and I couldn't get into it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9980644701452073153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11007370-caitlin-chciuk?shelf=summer-2013">summer-2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679495332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11625736747567106865">This is a very interesting book. I am a huge fan of the OUAT TV show, so when I heard they were writing a novel based on the series, I was quite excited. The book only covers season 1 -- I'm looking forward to the second book. The book was pretty true to the show, but missed some key backstories -- Sidney Glass, for example, was made to just look like he's in love with Regina; that backstory is not covered. I liked that the chapters lined up with the episodes, but I think that if they wanted to </span>
  <span id="freeText11625736747567106865" style="display:none">This is a very interesting book. I am a huge fan of the OUAT TV show, so when I heard they were writing a novel based on the series, I was quite excited. The book only covers season 1 -- I'm looking forward to the second book. The book was pretty true to the show, but missed some key backstories -- Sidney Glass, for example, was made to just look like he's in love with Regina; that backstory is not covered. I liked that the chapters lined up with the episodes, but I think that if they wanted to switch it up a bit, they could have done different chapters in different times. Instead, they cover different time periods in the same chapters, much like the show does in the episodes. Overall it was pretty good; I read it in a day (I think if you have the background knowledge from watching the show, it's an easy read). </span>
  <a data-text-id="11625736747567106865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1414550584278172151">While I love the show and really wanted to love this book, I didn't. It is all well and good to be a quick, easy read but I think it was something of a cheap job to do the chapters whole-cloth from the episodes. I understand that they didn't want to add anything, and that's perfectly fine, but the transitions that are effective on TV just didn't work in text. If I wasn't a faithful series watcher I would have gotten lost at some points because there was no common thread. In text form it also mad</span>
  <span id="freeText1414550584278172151" style="display:none">While I love the show and really wanted to love this book, I didn't. It is all well and good to be a quick, easy read but I think it was something of a cheap job to do the chapters whole-cloth from the episodes. I understand that they didn't want to add anything, and that's perfectly fine, but the transitions that are effective on TV just didn't work in text. If I wasn't a faithful series watcher I would have gotten lost at some points because there was no common thread. In text form it also made the show seem ridiculous, the characters flat, and the storyline cliche. I also wonder how the choose the style for the book because the show straddles that lines between children and adult at 8pm... The book didn't work for me. </span>

<div id="review_2576812001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576812001" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3075378-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303174580p2/3075378.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3075378-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3075378-erin?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3075378-erin?shelf=digital">digital</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3075378-erin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3075378-erin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3075378-erin?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576812001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15872008007015530565">I don't often read novelizations, but I found myself enjoying this.<br/>The familiar feeling of being back in Storybrooke, but being able to actually know the thoughts and emotions of the people as they are going through the first adventure was, well it felt like an Easter egg. Don't get me wrong, all the amazing actors and actresses in OUaT brought those feelings and emotions across their performances, but this is just... Different. <br/>Also there is no dichotomy between the onscreen characters, and the</span>
  <span id="freeText15872008007015530565" style="display:none">I don't often read novelizations, but I found myself enjoying this.<br />The familiar feeling of being back in Storybrooke, but being able to actually know the thoughts and emotions of the people as they are going through the first adventure was, well it felt like an Easter egg. Don't get me wrong, all the amazing actors and actresses in OUaT brought those feelings and emotions across their performances, but this is just... Different. <br />Also there is no dichotomy between the onscreen characters, and the written ones so that makes it just that much more immersing. <br />Okay, so that was written just after I started reading it.<br />Now that I've finished, I... don't want to say that I am disappointed, but I think I would have been happier with less rehashing of season 1, and more of a new story. Something we didn't get to see in season 1. You know, more slice of life type stuff with a plot.<br />This was literally just Snow/Mary Margaret and Emma's plots from S 1, and no one elses. <br />It was also a lot of telling instead of showing. I'm not saying it was bad, but there were times it felt like just trying to move to the next chapter as quickly and succinctly as possible without any description. <br />Even saying all that, I did enjoy it and makes me want to go back and binge watch all the seasons all over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15872008007015530565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6463535590646013903">I enjoyed this. As a fan of Once Upon A Time, it was fun to read the first season in a novel form. <div id="review_1056830418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7595197-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583993955p2/7595197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1056830418?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/7595197-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7595197-amanda?shelf=my-five-star-favourites">my-five-star-favourites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1056830418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2662314712675304411">Once upon a time is just like the TV series! Obviously there isn’t enough time to go through all the characters backgrounds like in the TV series, otherwise you'd need an extra 400 to 600 pages. The story covers the basic characters backgrounds like Snow White and Prince charming, and Snow White and Red riding hood. You also learn about the Evil Queens relationship with Snow White and why they hate each other so much. You also learn about Snow White and the seven dwarf's. Henry fills Emma in on </span>
  <span id="freeText2662314712675304411" style="display:none">Once upon a time is just like the TV series! Obviously there isn’t enough time to go through all the characters backgrounds like in the TV series, otherwise you'd need an extra 400 to 600 pages. The story covers the basic characters backgrounds like Snow White and Prince charming, and Snow White and Red riding hood. You also learn about the Evil Queens relationship with Snow White and why they hate each other so much. You also learn about Snow White and the seven dwarf's. Henry fills Emma in on the other characters throughout the book, like Rumpelstiltskin and Jiminy cricket and other fairy tale characters. I found the book very similar to the TV series which i love! It's almost word for word, and i love that. My favourite characters are Regina (The Evil Queen) Mr Gold (Rumpelstiltskin) Mary Margaret (Snow White) and Henry and Emma. I love the Evil Queen and Rumpelstiltskin the best in the TV series, i love how they take two bad guys and make you love them so much. The Evil Queen has killed many people and a lot of people still hate her and fear her, but as the series goes on you begin to love her even though she's a bad guy. And who doesn't love Rumpelstiltskin with his mad cackling and crazy giggles? He's a pain in the ass but he'll get you what you want...for a price of course! And i loved how Henry was in this book, he's a cute little guy brimming with curiosity and he loves his fairy tales. He tries to convince Emma that all the stories in his book are real, which are actually the stories of Snow White and Prince charming and the Evil Queen in fairy tale land. This book is definitely worth 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2662314712675304411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15840996894337826064" style="display:none">I love <i>OUAT</i>. I wanted to love this book as much as I love the show, but that ended up being impossible. So much was left out, which I could have overlooked, except for the fact that it also added absolutely nothing new. What was the point of even reading this? I could have popped in the DVD and enjoyed season 1 in its fullest, most vivid form.<br /><br />To make matters worse, the scarcity wasn't even very well written. I don't blame the author on this front, as I assume she was simply doing the bidding of ABC. The magic at the heart of this show was completely absent. There was no feeling behind the words, especially in the rushed ending. The ending of season 1 packed such an emotional punch, it had to be hard to zap the book of every ounce of that.<br /><br />I'm just sad I spent $11 on this instead of putting the money toward buying season 2.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5748551-chandni?shelf=zz-reading-bingo-ya-2014">zz-reading-bingo-ya-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5748551-chandni?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5748551-chandni?shelf=unhaul">unhaul</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704403329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6402066274153602744"><b>2.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>This was a really superficial novelization of Season 1. It was lacking a lot of the charm that the show has because we only saw things from Emma and Mary Margaret's point of view. We didn't see the other things that were going on with Gold or Regina, which really made it hard to connect with the book. It was also missing the episodes that weren't centered around the core characters for the same reason.<br/><br/>Mediocre at best, but at least it refreshed my memory about some of the plot points.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ofA3ZroNbD3vzax+KAPOXKnZQ0V3KpRe2gfl320y249ipqZJpdqPU7OOEfXpjQ3ImJPsmhfVe5ZIFSGkRq8GPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kqWmXM7/pT9LIJLNSdOwJVQW5tPq2l0rMUSdojI+4W5R8zdz0ShGURdjL0aIXXOxZVxJDIolsuOjVlnZGaM83Q==')})
  }

While the novel\'s plotline (a struggling New York City private eye accepts a lucrative assignment to track down a real estate magnate\'s wayward identical twin, only to be sucked into an unfathomably deep conspiracy) has no obvious links to the television show, there are countless tantalizing references throughout that will have hard-core fans of Lost speculating for months. (For example, the wealthy man looking for his brother is named Clifford Widmore, and a prominent organization renting space in his flagship building is the Hanso Foundation.) There are numerous references to John Locke, numerology, and purgatory, which many fans have speculated is actually where the show is set: The characters are all dead and working their way toward redemption. An anagram for the fictional author Gary Troup is, by the way, Purgatory. \n\nBad Twin is intimately connected to Lost, but it is also a highly entertaining whodunit reminiscent of timeless noir gems by masters like Ed McBain, Donald E. Westlake, and Lawrence Block. Fans of the television show will devour this novel, as will any mystery fan who can get past the obvious marketing tie-in.
